Weekly leading indicators
IndicatorDefinitionWeekly guardrail
Sessions (all channels)Total tracked sessions>=500 sessions by week 4
Sitewide CVR (7-day trailing)Orders / sessions>=1.4% target; 0.9% floor
Paid CAC (7-day trailing)Paid spend / paid orders<=EUR 25 by week 6; <= gross profit/order always
Blended CAC (7-day trailing)Paid spend / all orders<=EUR 15 by week 4; <=EUR 13 by week 8+
Payment success rateSuccessful payments / payment attempts>=97% (decision-valid at >=100 attempts)
Return rate (30-day trailing)Returned orders / shipped orders<=7% (decision-valid at >=25 shipped orders)
Kill/Pivot thresholds (enforced)
  1. If paid CAC is above observed gross profit/order for 7 consecutive days, pivot to retargeting-only acquisition.
  2. If sitewide CVR is below 0.9% after >=500 sessions in a 7-day window, stop spend expansion and run conversion fixes first.
  3. If return rate exceeds 7% after >=25 shipped orders, hold growth and remediate compatibility/fit issues before re-scaling.
  4. If payment success drops below 97% after >=100 attempts, pause traffic increases until checkout reliability recovers.

  • Trigger hold/fix: any gate fails or denominator threshold not met.
  • Trigger pivot: same gate fails 2 consecutive weekly cycles.

90-Day Forecast v2T2 ¬∑ 200 lines

90-Day Forecast v2

T2 ¬∑ 200 lines

docs/business-os/strategy/HEAD/headband-90-day-launch-forecast-v2.user.md

HEAD 90-Day Launch Forecast (v2)

Input Packet

  • Business: HEAD
  • Idea: products for people with cochlear implants
  • Product: headbands to hold cochlear implants in place
  • Target customer (initial): people with cochlear implants
  • Channel: own site (primary)
  • Budget constraint: stock already purchased; ad budget to be derived from TAM and market data
  • Stock timeline: inventory already purchased (near-term launch-ready)
  • Horizon: 90 days

Launch Surface Mode

  • Mode used in this run: website-live
  • Metric set used: sessions, conversion, orders, revenue, margin, CAC

A) Executive Summary

  1. Best available published estimate found for Italy is ~17,000 cochlear-implant users (0.03% of population).
  2. Italy has annual new-user flow: one Italian clinical overview reports ~1,400 cochlear implants and auditory brainstem implants in 2022.
  3. Direct Italian ecommerce competitors sell retention headbands in roughly EUR 18.00-EUR 28.80; adjacent EU sellers reach EUR 12.00.
  4. Most practical initial ICP is parents/caregivers of children ~6 months-6 years where retention need is explicit in competitor positioning.
  5. Secondary ICPs after initial validation: school-age children and active adults (sport/movement retention use cases).
  6. Directional owned-site conversion benchmark for Italy cited in research: ~0.90%-2.2%.
  7. Italy return incidence benchmark cited: 5.7% average; 7.4% apparel/sport/accessories; 5.5% health/wellbeing.
  8. Paid acquisition economics are tight for low-AOV single-SKU launch; use paid for precision learning, not brute-force scale.
  9. With small TAM, niche awareness can be saturated with modest budget, but cold paid cannot be primary growth engine unless AOV/repeat behavior improves.
  10. Multiple payment methods are required for conversion hygiene in Italy.
  11. EU/Italy distance-selling withdrawal rights (14 days) must be treated as mandatory operating baseline.
  12. Proposed 90-day base target: around 110 net orders (P50) with immediate week-1/week-2 recalibration.

B) Competitor Benchmark Table

Interpretation notes:

  • Base case assumes blended owned-site conversion inside directional Italy benchmark band.
  • Return assumptions are anchored to Italian incidence benchmarks and should be re-estimated with observed week-1/week-2 data.
  • Paid cost assumptions are directional and require immediate validation.

D) Proposed Goals

Primary ICP recommendation
  • Parents/caregivers of children roughly 6 months-6 years with cochlear implants (daily retention need during play/school).
Secondary ICPs (after first validation loop)
  • School-age children with movement/sport use cases.
  • Active adults with sport/heat/sweat retention use cases.
90-day targets
  • Commercial target: ~110 net orders in 90 days (aligned with P50 net orders).
  • Revenue target: ~EUR 3,000 net revenue in 90 days (aligned with P50 net revenue).
  • Learning target: >=6,000 total sessions by day 90, with clean tracking by channel and landing page.
  • Paid efficiency guardrail: blended CAC <=EUR 13 by day 60 and paid CAC <=EUR 25 by day 90 unless AOV increases via bundles.
  • Returns target: <=7% return rate.
  • Effort allocation target: preserve ~95/5 split (direct launch execution vs CMS migration).
Weekly leading indicators
  • Traffic: sessions, source mix, landing-page split.
  • Funnel: product-page view rate, add-to-cart, checkout start, checkout completion.
  • Conversion: weekly CVR and CVR by channel.
  • Economics: AOV, paid CAC, gross profit per order net of returns.
  • Trust/payment: payment method split and payment success rate.
  • Customer insight: weekly conversation count, top objections, top purchase reasons.
  • Quality: return reasons, fit issues, compatibility support requests.

G) First 14-Day Validation Plan

  1. Confirm inventory readiness and fulfill order -&gt; shipped median <=48h.
  2. Ensure multiple payment methods are live and tested end-to-end.
  3. Publish clear Italian withdrawal/returns flow aligned to 14-day baseline.
  4. Publish compatibility/fit decision aid before scaling paid.
  5. Run capped two-channel tests:
  • high-intent paid search
  • paid social retargeting + focused interest tests
  1. Track CPC, CVR, paid CAC daily.
  2. Decision thresholds (first pass):
  • if paid CAC > gross profit/order for 7 consecutive days, reduce paid to retargeting only
  • if sitewide CVR <0.9% after >=500 sessions, prioritize landing-page and trust fixes before spend increase
  1. Tag every return reason from day 1.
  2. Use hearing-awareness dates as early content/outreach pulses.

Market Intelligence (Resolved)

T2 ¬∑ 202 lines

docs/business-os/market-research/HEAD/2026-02-12-market-intelligence.user.md

Market Intelligence Pack: HEAD - Cochlear Implant Headbands in Italy

A) Executive Summary

  • Italy cochlear implant installed base is meaningful but niche: about 17,000 users.
  • Italian procedure flow is material and appears to have grown over time.
  • Headband retention products are clearly active in Italian specialist retail.
  • Observed visible price corridor is broad (roughly low-teens EUR to premium ~EUR65).
  • Etsy and Amazon surfaces show established marketplace behavior for this category.
  • Research signal suggests strong marketplace demand capture potential; operating channel authority is decision-bound in DEC-HEAD-CH-01.
  • Segment sequencing should start with highest urgency users (caregivers/children), then sport-active users, then daily-comfort adults.
  • Economics can work but are highly sensitive to conversion, CAC, and especially returns.
  • Checkout/payments must align with Italian buyer expectations (cards/wallets, with PayPal strong).
  • Regulatory boundary risk is material: accessory-to-medical-device interpretation under MDR can change obligations.
  • GPSR applies, so safety/traceability requirements are live.
  • Core recommendation: validation-led launch, disciplined claims, and aggressive early measurement.

B) Business Context and Assumptions

  • Business intent: B2C brand for cochlear implant users, starting with retention headbands.
  • Launch surface: pre-website.
  • Stock posture: initial stock already purchased; assume near-term sellable availability (<=14 days) until exact date is confirmed.
  • Budget posture: avoid large blind paid spend; set from TAM constraints and early measured economics.
  • Operating posture: 95/5 split toward direct sales execution vs CMS migration.

C) Market Size and Demand Signals

SignalCurrent read
Installed base~17,000 CI users in Italy (observed in cited source set)
Procedure trendLong-run growth signal present in cited population study
Specialist retail presenceMultiple Italian SKUs with explicit sport/kids positioning
Marketplace breadthEtsy query indicates large relevant listing surface
Category seriousnessAmazon category rank evidence exists for retention bands
Macro ecommerce contextItaly ecommerce volume large enough to support focused niche capture

Seasonality hypothesis for validation:

  • Demand may skew with sport/outdoor activity periods and school-cycle moments.
  • Validate with short cohort/creative tests tagged by use-case.

D) Competitor and Substitute Map (Italy-first)

Direct competitors:

  • PowerAiD / SmartEAR family (universal, sport, children variants).
  • Amazon direct-value listings (adjustable anti-loss bands).
  • Etsy independent sellers with sizing/sport variants.

Adjacent:

  • Protective sleeves/tether products positioned for weather/sweat/anti-loss use.

Substitutes:

  • OEM retention ecosystems (Cochlear/MED-EL accessory stacks).

Strategic implication:

  • Differentiate on compatibility clarity, trust/support, and fit reliability rather than only price.

E) Pricing Benchmarks (Observed Range)

Observed pricing surfaces suggest:

  • Entry/value: mid-teens EUR.
  • Core specialist tier: high-teens to low-thirties EUR.
  • Premium protective tier: up to ~EUR65.

Practical launch implication:

  • Position a clear hero band in core tier, with evidence-backed reason to prefer over low-end alternatives.

F) Segment Sequence and JTBD

Primary segment (first):

  • Parents/caregivers of young children using CI processors.
  • JTBD: keep processor secure during play/school while maintaining usable microphone placement.

Secondary segment:

  • Active/sport users (children/teens/adults), including off-the-ear processor users.
  • JTBD: secure fit during movement/sweat with anti-loss confidence.

Tertiary segment:

  • Adults focused on discreet daily comfort and confidence.

G) Unit Economics Priors (Validation Stage)

Directional priors for early planning:

  • Single-unit price corridor: roughly EUR18-EUR32 for core tier.
  • AOV potential: improved by bundle mechanics.
  • CVR prior: low-single-digit range pending measured data.
  • Returns prior: material risk driver and must be actively controlled.
  • CAC prior: highly uncertain pre-launch; must be measured in week 1-2.
  • Margin prior: feasible only if fit/returns/support friction are managed.

H) Channel Strategy Inputs (First 90 Days)

Decision authority:

  • Channel-surface decision is governed by docs/business-os/strategy/HEAD/decisions/DEC-HEAD-CH-01.user.md.
  • Current decision state (Active): own-site DTC primary, with constrained marketplace probes.

Research-derived channel inputs:

  1. Marketplace probes should prioritize Etsy first; Amazon only if operationally feasible.
  2. Minimal DTC trust/FAQ/compatibility surface remains mandatory for denominator-quality learning.
  3. Community/association-led trust channels remain low-CAC opportunities.
  4. Paid expansion should follow evidence-gate pass conditions only.

I) Website Design Implications

Minimum website requirements for launch:

  • Use-case-led IA (Kids / Sport / Daily).
  • Compatibility selector and sizing guidance.
  • PDP clarity on fit, mic exposure considerations, and care instructions.
  • Clear returns/withdrawal and support pathways.
  • Italy-suitable payment options (cards + PayPal minimum).
  • Privacy/cookie compliance from day one.

J) Product Design Implications

Must-have design constraints:

  • Secure retention without microphone obstruction.
  • Unilateral and bilateral wearing support.
  • Child-safe retention approach where relevant.
  • Explicit sizing model tied to head circumference.
  • Clear compatibility mapping by processor family.

Failure modes to test early:

  • Slippage under sweat/motion.
  • Fit discomfort/pressure.
  • Mic interference due to placement.
  • Fastener durability/usability issues.

K) Regulatory and Claims Constraints

Key constraints:

  • MDR accessory boundary risk must be handled carefully (claims + intended use language matter).
  • GPSR obligations apply.
  • Textile labeling obligations apply.
  • Distance-selling withdrawal rights and legal guarantee obligations must be reflected in policy and operations.
  • Child-safety hazards (for cords/attachments) must be proactively designed out or mitigated.

Red lines:

  1. No medical efficacy claims.
  2. No unsafe child-oriented attachment design.
  3. No DTC launch without compliant withdrawal/returns/legal identity setup.

L) Proposed 90-Day Outcome Contract

OutcomeTarget window
First paid ordersDay 14 threshold test
Repeatable weekly salesBy Day 60 with consistency gate
Return-rate controlBy Day 90 with reason-coded tracking
Positive contribution trendBy Day 90, pre-ads contribution guardrail
Compliance readiness for full site-liveBy Day 45 checklist completion
Owned audience growthBy Day 90 audience baseline established

M) First-14-Day Validation Plan

Core tests:

  1. Marketplace intent test (kids + sport SKU setup).
  2. Messaging split test (kids pain vs sport pain).
  3. Fit uncertainty reduction test (sizing + compatibility UX).
  4. Bundle uptake test (2-pack/3-pack economics).
  5. Community trust-channel test.
  6. Micro-pilot returns risk test.

Each test should have explicit pass/fail thresholds and a re-forecast trigger.

N) Assumptions Register (Condensed)

Highest-impact assumptions:

  • Stock readiness timing.
  • Segment priority correctness.
  • Price corridor fit for first buyers.
  • Early CVR/CAC viability.
  • Returns controllability.
  • Regulatory classification path viability under chosen claims language.

O) Risk Register (Condensed)

Top risks:

  • MDR accessory interpretation risk.
  • Returns eroding contribution.
  • Marketplace competition compressing margin.
  • Over-claim risk on sport/sweat/water performance.
  • Child safety hazards in attachment design.
  • Payment friction reducing conversion.

P) Source List (Provided in Research Payload)

Primary source families included in the provided payload:

  • Italian clinical and population data sources.
  • Italian specialist ecommerce product pages.
  • Etsy/Amazon/eBay market surfaces.
  • OEM accessory pages.
  • Italy ecommerce benchmark publications.
  • EU/Italy regulatory texts and guidance (GPSR, MDR, textile labeling, withdrawal rights, guarantees, privacy/cookies).

HEAD Site Upgrade Brief

1) Business Outcome Frame

  • Convert cochlear-implant headband demand into reliable first sales in Italy, then repeatable weekly sales.
  • Reduce wrong-fit/wrong-device purchases through compatibility and sizing clarity.
  • Decision links unlocked:
  • DEC-HEAD-01: scale paid demand generation beyond precision/retargeting.
  • DEC-HEAD-02: expand into add-ons (jewellery/retention accessories) after core PDP conversion is stable.

2) Existing Site Baseline

  • Launch-surface mode: pre-website.
  • Core constraint: speed-to-first-sales; avoid heavy CMS dependency in first cycle.
  • Current friction risks to remove before scale:
  • compatibility ambiguity,
  • size/fit uncertainty,
  • weak trust signals for a medical-adjacent category,
  • checkout/payment friction for Italian buyers.

3) Reference Sites

  • PowerAid (Italy): direct local benchmark for pricing, sizing tables, and CI-retention copy.
  • SmartEar (EU): strong compatibility-led PDP structure with clear trust stack.
  • hearinghenry: CI-specific story-led positioning, especially caregiver/toddler segment.
  • Deafmetal: identity-plus-retention framing for adult/teen confidence and add-on economics.
  • BAHA Accessories UK: robust options architecture (single/bilateral, age/size tiers, add-ons).
  • CI Retention Solutions: bundle and multi-buy mechanics.
  • MED-EL / Advanced Bionics: manufacturer-grade compatibility and functional language benchmark.

6) Design Implications

  • Information architecture:
  • Home with ICP split (Caregivers/Kids, Sport/Active, Daily Comfort).
  • Core PDP with compatibility + sizing above the fold.
  • Dedicated compatibility guide and sizing guide pages.
  • Support/FAQ, legal/returns, and provider page.
  • Page/component implications:
  • Compatibility matrix component.
  • Size selector with circumference helper.
  • Trust strip near CTA (payments, returns, shipping, reviews).
  • Sticky mobile purchase CTA.
  • Copy/messaging implications:
  • Use-case language: loss prevention, fit stability, sweat/sport stability.
  • Avoid medical efficacy claims.
  • Clarify microphone-safe wear guidance where true.
  • Trust/support implications:
  • Fast support entrypoint (including messaging channel).
  • Clear delivery windows and returns workflow.

7) Technical Implications

  • Reusable platform primitives to use:
  • product option components,
  • trust/payment iconography blocks,
  • FAQ/accordion patterns,
  • analytics event hooks for funnel steps.
  • New build requirements:
  • compatibility data model keyed by processor family/model,
  • sizing helper logic + content management for fit guides,
  • event instrumentation for compatibility/sizing interactions.
  • Testing and observability implications:
  • Unit tests for compatibility and size logic.
  • Integration tests for add-to-cart with options.
  • E2E tests for checkout path and policy visibility.
  • KPI logging for CVR, checkout drop-off, and return reasons.

Brand DossierT2 ¬∑ 151 lines

Brand Dossier

T2 ¬∑ 151 lines

docs/business-os/strategy/HEAD/brand-identity.user.md

Headband (CochlearFit) ‚Äî Brand Dossier

> Draft status. Token values are not duplicated in this document. When the theme package > is created, the single source of truth will be packages/themes/cochlearfit/src/tokens.ts. > This document records why tokens should be chosen, not what values they hold. > All TBD fields require operator input or market research before this dossier can advance to Active.

Audience

Primary: Adults and parents of children with cochlear implants in Italy. Age range TBD ‚Äî cochlear implant users span from infants to elderly; the head-worn accessory category skews toward parents purchasing for children and adult women purchasing for themselves. Italy TAM estimate: ~17,000 cochlear-implant users (niche).

Secondary: TBD ‚Äî gift purchasers (family members, audiologists recommending accessories).

Device: TBD ‚Äî mobile-first assumed based on Italian e-commerce norms, but must be validated with first-party analytics once live.

Context: Likely discovery via search (high-intent, problem-aware) and peer community referral (cochlear implant communities, parenting forums). Purchasing decision is practical + emotional: does it fit my device? will it stay on? does it look good? Trust, compatibility evidence, and return policy clarity are decision-critical.

Key insight: The audience is defined by a medical device (cochlear implant), not purely by demographics. Compatibility and fit are purchase-blockers, not just preferences. Tone must be matter-of-fact and reassuring, not medicalized.

Personality

  • Reassuring, not clinical
  • Practical, not purely aspirational
  • Approachable, not technical or jargon-heavy
  • Inclusive, not niche-stigmatizing (normalizes wearing a headband, doesn't over-emphasize disability)
  • Warm, not corporate

> TBD ‚Äî Validate personality direction with 3‚Äì5 customer conversations or community feedback before advancing to Active.

Visual Identity

Color Palette

> TBD ‚Äî No design work has been done for CochlearFit. The following are directional notes only. > A dedicated /lp-design-spec session + theme package creation is required before Active status.

RoleToken (proposed)Rationale
PrimaryTBDShould feel warm and approachable without clinical/medical coldness. Avoid blue-white (medical). Consider soft earth tones or muted pastels. Validate against accessibility + competitor differentiation.
Primary softTBDTinted background for cards and highlights
AccentTBDComplementary to primary; avoid red/orange (urgency reads as alarm in medical contexts)
BackgroundTBDClean, light ‚Äî not stark white (cold), not cream (dated)

Palette mood: TBD ‚Äî candidate direction: warm neutral + 1 distinctive accent. Avoid the cold clinical look of medical equipment. Avoid the aggressive energy of sports accessories. Aim for "everyday lifestyle that happens to accommodate a medical device."

Typography
RoleToken (proposed)Rationale
Body + headingsTBDReadable, friendly, not too geometric (engineer feel). Consider humanist sans-serif. Italian market: ensure good display at moderate sizes.
MonospaceN/A ‚Äî no dev-facing UI

Token Rationale

> Token rationale will be populated when the theme package is created. This section is a placeholder.

TokenDesign rationale
_(all TBD)_Theme package packages/themes/cochlearfit/ does not yet exist. Populate when created via /lp-design-spec.
Imagery Direction
  • Do: Real product photography showing fit on head (over cochlear implant worn correctly). Lifestyle photography with natural lighting. Inclusive representation ‚Äî show range of ages, hair types, and cochlear implant processor types.
  • Don't: Stock photography of generic hair accessories. Over-medicalized imagery (hospital settings, devices isolated on white). Imagery that emphasizes disability over lifestyle.

> TBD ‚Äî Validate imagery direction against competitor positioning and community feedback.

Voice & Tone

Writing Style
  • Sentence length: Short and direct. Customers often have practical questions; answer them quickly.
  • Formality: Conversational but professional. Not casual-slang; not formal-medical.
  • Technical level: Acknowledge the device (cochlear implant) without jargon. Use plain names for processor brands (Cochlear Nucleus, Advanced Bionics, MED-EL) when compatibility is stated ‚Äî customers know their own device.
  • Italian localization: Primary market is Italian. Italian copy should feel native, not translated. Warmth in Italian differs from English warmth ‚Äî shorter sentences, direct address.
Key Phrases

> TBD ‚Äî Validate with customer interviews. Directional suggestions:

  • "Fits your processor" (compatibility-first framing)
  • "Made for everyday wear" (normalizes the use case)
  • "Your fit, your style" (practical + personal)
Words to Avoid

> TBD ‚Äî Validate with customer/community feedback. Initial candidates:

  • Medical jargon ("implant-compatible device interface")
  • Stigmatizing language ("hide your processor", "disguise")
  • Overpromising fit language without evidence ("fits all processors" if not verified)

Signature Patterns

> TBD ‚Äî No application has been built yet. Patterns will be added as /lp-design-spec identifies them during feature work.

_First pattern to define: product compatibility display component (which processor brands/models this headband fits ‚Äî this is the primary conversion trust element)._

HEAD DISCOVERY-03 ‚Äî Option Selection

Options Evaluated (7 total)

OptionDescriptionDecisionRationale
1 ‚Äî Textile lifestyle accessory brandMulti-SKU headbands, pouches, and patch accessories for CI wearers‚úÖ SHORTLISTEDNo MDR risk under intended-purpose framing; operator inventory purchased; Italy demand confirmed; broadens into range over time
2 ‚Äî Digital app (processor management)Companion app for CI wearers‚ùå ELIMINATEDHigh dev investment; regulated boundary risk; no operator expertise; long time-to-first-sale
3 ‚Äî CE-marked medical device accessoryDevice that requires MDR certification‚ùå ELIMINATEDMDR "intended purpose" compliance requires clinical/regulatory pathway; fatal for solo operator
4 ‚Äî Bespoke/custom serviceCustom-made CI accessories per order‚ùå ELIMINATEDUnscalable at low AOV; impossible to systematize CAC/CVR measurement
5 ‚Äî Generic children's accessoriesNon-CI-specific headbands‚ùå ELIMINATEDLoses ICP specificity and pricing power; no differentiation
6 ‚Äî Subscription boxMonthly CI-accessory subscription‚ùå ELIMINATEDPremature for pre-PMF; requires established repeat buyer base first
7 ‚Äî Marketplace aggregatorCurate other brands' CI accessories‚ùå ELIMINATEDNo brand building; low margin; no proprietary demand signal

Decision

Option 1 selected. Two corrections applied from live research: (1) Cochlear's own accessory stack is more complete than assumed ‚Äî must differentiate on fit variety, style, and bundle value; (2) MDR "intended purpose" risk is material ‚Äî all claims must be positioned as lifestyle/comfort, never therapeutic efficacy.

S2B Offer Design

T2 ¬∑ 2026-02-20 ¬∑ confidence: medium-high

docs/business-os/startup-baselines/HEAD-offer.md

HEAD Offer Design

ICP

Parents/caregivers of children (6 months‚Äì6 years) with cochlear implant processors in Italy. Secondary: active/sport adult wearers. Tertiary: school-age children and daily-comfort adults.

Positioning

"Secure wear for busy days. Calmer routines. Made to be worn proudly." ‚Äî Non-medicalised, lifestyle-first. Differentiates on Italian register, compatibility clarity, and emotional reassurance for parents.

MVP Product Stack

SKUDescriptionPrice (EUR)Priority
HB-SINGLESingle retention headband (colour options)18‚Äì24Hero SKU
HB-MULTIMulti-pack (3 headbands, mixed colours)45‚Äì55AOV driver
HB-KITSchool kit (headband + organiser pouch)59‚Äì79Higher-margin bundle
POUCH-ORGProcessor organiser pouch22‚Äì28Accessory cross-sell
PATCH-PACKAdhesive patch packs (sweat/sport)12‚Äì18Repeat-purchase item

Key Claims (Non-Medical)

  • Secure hold during play, school, sport ‚Äî without obscuring the microphone
  • Sized for real head circumferences (chart on PDP)
  • Soft, washable, Italian-designed
  • Compatible with [named processor families]

Objection Handling

  • "My child already has the manufacturer's band" ‚Üí Ours is softer / more colours / purpose-built for play
  • "EUR 18 for a headband?" ‚Üí Compatibility guide shows why fit quality matters; show return rate as proof point once available
  • "Is this medically certified?" ‚Üí Lifestyle accessory; not a medical device; this is a comfort and security product

Messaging Hierarchy

docs/business-os/strategy/HEAD/messaging-hierarchy.user.md

HEAD Messaging Hierarchy

Core Message

"Secure wear for busy days. Calmer routines. Made to be worn proudly."

Three Pillars

PillarClaimEvidence / support
1 ‚Äî Secure Everyday WearStays in place during play, school, sport without obscuring the microphoneCompatibility matrix, sizing chart, use-case photography
2 ‚Äî Calmer RoutinesReduces morning friction and anxiety for caregivers and childrenCommunity evidence; comfort failure mode research; testimonials post-launch
3 ‚Äî Personal StyleColours and designs made to be noticed positively, not hiddenColour range; lifestyle photography; gifting angle for school/activities

Claims Guardrails (MDR compliance)

  • Always: lifestyle, comfort, security framing
  • Never: therapeutic efficacy, medical device claims, clinical outcome language
  • Avoid: "improves hearing", "protects the device medically", "recommended by audiologists" (without evidence)

Status: Draft ‚Äî awaiting brand name clearance to finalize tone and Italian copy register.

Week 2 Gate Dry-Run

docs/business-os/strategy/HEAD/2026-02-11-week2-gate-dry-run.user.md

HEAD Week-2 Gate Review ‚Äî Dry-Run (Synthetic)

Purpose

Validate that the HEAD launch decision process is configured correctly and adds decision value before the website is launch-ready.

Inputs Used (Synthetic)

Assumed 7-day trailing observed metrics:

MetricDry-run valueGate
CVR1.24%>= 1.1%
Contribution/order (pre ads)EUR 11.20baseline
Blended CACEUR 8.10<= 75% of contribution/order (<= EUR 8.40)
Refund rate10.4%<= 9%
On-time ship rate96.3%>= 95%
Payment success rate97.6%>= 97%

Gate Evaluation

GateResultNotes
CVR >= 1.1%PASSconversion is acceptable
CAC <= 75% of contribution/orderPASSefficiency within threshold
Refund <= 9%FAILreturn burden too high
On-time ship >= 95%PASSfulfillment reliability acceptable
Payment success >= 97%PASScheckout reliability acceptable

Decision rule outcome:

  • NO-GO (scale hold) because one mandatory gate failed.
  • Prescribed action: fix-first mode (hold cold scaling, keep retargeting, fix fit/comfort and expectation mismatch, re-test in 7 days).

Quality Check ‚Äî Is This Setup Right and Valuable?

Rubric
DimensionScore (0-5)Why
Deterministic decisioning5.0hard gates create repeatable outcomes
Actionability4.5direct fallback mode is defined
Margin protection4.5CAC is tied to contribution capacity
Product-market signal quality4.0refund gate exposes fit/value mismatch early
Data burden realism3.5requires disciplined instrumentation cadence
Anti-vanity bias5.0avoids scaling on sessions alone

Weighted quality score:

  • 4.4 / 5.0 (88%)
Value Demonstrated by This Dry-Run
  • Topline funnel metrics look passable, but refund burden blocks safe scaling.
  • The gate system catches this and forces corrective action before spend expansion.
  • This prevents avoidable CAC burn while core offer clarity is still unstable.

Gaps Found in Process Setup

  1. Region/tax model is still assumption-led and not locked. Open.
  2. No explicit statistical confidence treatment yet for small weekly samples. Open.
  3. Owner map and remediation SLA now exist in forecast v1. Resolved.

Recommended Next Actions

  1. Run a fit/comfort expectation audit on PDP and ad creative.
  2. Add return-reason tags and require weekly root-cause review.
  3. Re-run week-2 gate pack with updated funnel and returns data.

Conclusion

The process is useful and materially protective, but currently constrained by unresolved region/tax assumptions and missing variance-aware evaluation.

PET Dog Accessories ‚Äî Offer Design

Executive summary: A premium dog lifestyle accessories brand targeting urban millennial female dog owners who treat their dog as a lifestyle extension. Product 1 is a mini Birkin-style poop bag holder with leash clip at ‚Ç¨80 ‚Äî positioned between Atlas Pet Co ($45 craft) and LISH London (¬£65 leather), well below Pagerie ($152). What makes this different: genuinely usable craft quality, a no-fault exchange policy (Pagerie's single biggest failure point), and a design that makes the walk feel put together. Brand scope is intentionally broad ‚Äî full dog lifestyle accessories line ‚Äî with the holder as the demand test product.

Section 1: ICP Segmentation

ICP-A: The Dog Mum (Primary ‚Äî 80% of launch buyers)

Demographics:

  • Age: 25‚Äì40
  • Location: urban centres (Milan, London, Barcelona, Amsterdam, Paris) ‚Äî cities with caf√© culture

and dog-welcome spaces; also coastal/resort towns where dogs are carried or walked in fashionable contexts

  • Income: ‚Ç¨35,000‚Äì‚Ç¨80,000 household (comfortably spending ‚Ç¨80 without a second thought on

something she loves, even if she'd pause at ‚Ç¨150)

  • Device: mobile-first; discovers via Instagram Reels, TikTok, Etsy search
  • She doesn't have children yet ‚Äî or has made a conscious choice. Her dog is her dog, not

the family pet.

Psychographics:

  • Values: aesthetics, quality over quantity, brand story, sustainability signals, Italian/

European craft. Not a logo-chaser ‚Äî more "quiet luxury" than status display.

  • Fear: looking like she "tried too hard" ‚Äî she wants to look effortlessly considered, not

ostentatious. She won't buy the ¬£300 Pagerie harness because it screams money. She'll buy the ‚Ç¨80 Italian leather holder because it looks like taste.

  • Aspiration: to be the version of herself on a walk that matches how she feels in the rest

of her life ‚Äî curated, intentional, well-dressed. Her dog is an extension of that.

  • Buying style: researches before buying (Instagram ‚Üí website ‚Üí Etsy ‚Üí reviews), makes

emotionally-driven decisions she then rationalises logically. Uses the word "splurge" to grant herself permission.

Jobs-to-be-done:

  • Functional: carry poop bags on a walk without it looking utilitarian or ugly
  • Emotional: feel put together ‚Äî "I'm the dog mum who has it together"
  • Social: earn compliments from strangers and community recognition in the dog-owner world

Buying triggers:

  • Sees a beautiful holder on someone else's dog at the park and asks "where did you get that?"
  • Gets a new dog / first dog ‚Äî the "setting up" purchase moment
  • Replaces a broken or ugly plastic dispenser that's been annoying her for months
  • Gifting occasion: dog's "birthday", new dog gift, Christmas self-treat
ICP-B: The Gift-Giver (Secondary ‚Äî ~20% of launch buyers)

Demographics:

  • Age: 28‚Äì55 (broader ‚Äî can be a parent, sibling, friend of the primary ICP)
  • Location: anywhere shipping reaches
  • Budget allocated: ‚Ç¨70‚Äì‚Ç¨100 (gift budget ‚Äî slightly less price-sensitive than a self-purchase

because "it's a gift")

Psychographics:

  • Buying for: someone who fits ICP-A exactly
  • Fear: getting something generic or cheap-looking when the recipient has "taste"
  • Aspiration: to be the friend who got the perfect gift ‚Äî not another candle or wine

Jobs-to-be-done:

  • Functional: find a high-quality, distinctive gift for a dog-owner friend
  • Emotional: be seen as the thoughtful, taste-edited giver
  • Social: strengthen the relationship through a demonstrably considered gift

Buying triggers:

  • Dog birthday (44% of dog owners buy birthday gifts for their pets)
  • New dog gift ("welcome to dog ownership")
  • Christmas / birthday ‚Äî "she already has everything but doesn't have this"
  • Recent break-up or life event where the dog is particularly important to the recipient

Section 3: Offer Structure

Core Offer

Product: Mini Birkin-style dog poop bag holder with brass leash clip

  • Materials: leather or high-quality leather-look body (same as HBAG line), brass-finish leash clip

hardware, magnetic clasp closure

  • Includes: 1 roll of poop bags (enough for the walk that tests the holder)
  • Dimensions: holds 1 standard roll of poop bags; designed for one-hand access
  • Attachment: clips to any standard dog lead, belt loop, or bag strap
  • Available: single colourway at launch (to be confirmed from /lp-offer brand palette work)

Price: ‚Ç¨80 (confirmed by Pete 2026-02-17)

Delivery: Italy-origin; EU + international shipping. Timeframe TBD from supplier.

Bundles / Tier Variants

At launch: single SKU (poop bag holder). No bundles pre-checkpoint.

Post-checkpoint candidate bundles (not in scope for demand test):

  • Dog Walk Set: holder + matching lead charm
  • Gift Set: holder + drawstring gift pouch + handwritten note card
Included Deliverables
  • Holder itself (with 1 roll of bags)
  • Tissue + ribbon packaging (positioned as giftable out of the box)
  • Handwritten note from maker (the Etsy emotional differentiator ‚Äî replicable at small scale)
  • Care card (leather/faux-leather care instructions)
Exclusions
  • No dog lead (holder clips to existing lead; leads are not sold at launch)
  • No personalisation at launch (name engraving, breed charm ‚Äî deferred to post-10 sales)
  • No subscription / auto-refill bags service
Guarantees
  • 30-day free exchange on any order (no fault required ‚Äî wrong colour, doesn't feel right,

changed mind). One exchange per order. This is the direct counter to Pagerie's fatal flaw.

  • Quality guarantee: if the hardware fails within 90 days of normal use, replacement at no cost.
Risk Reversals
  • Generous exchange policy removes the biggest premium purchase blocker
  • No sizing anxiety (leash clip design eliminates fit variables that plague harness/collar purchases)
  • "Try it on your walk" implicit: the stakes of a failed purchase are low (clip it on, use it once,

exchange if it's not right)

Section 4: Positioning One-Pager

Positioning Statement (Moore Template)
For urban millennial female dog owners, 25‚Äì40,
        who treat their dog as a lifestyle extension but refuse to carry something ugly on their walks,
        [BRAND NAME] is a premium dog lifestyle accessories brand
        that turns the most unglamorous moment of dog ownership into something that looks considered ‚Äî
        unlike Pagerie (too expensive, terrible returns) or Lucy & Co (too casual, wrong aesthetic),
        because we craft our accessories from the same leather body as a mini Birkin,
        at ‚Ç¨80, with a 30-day no-fault exchange.
Category

Existing category: premium/artisan dog accessories. We are not creating a new category ‚Äî we are occupying the white space between accessible-fashion (Lucy & Co at $14) and ultra-luxury (Pagerie at $152). The gap is real, documented, and currently occupied only by LISH London (¬£65, operational failures) and Atlas Pet Co ($45, function-not-fashion focus).

Competitive Frame

Customers compare us to:

  1. Other Etsy artisan sellers ($25‚Äì60 range) ‚Äî our primary frame at launch
  2. LISH London (¬£65) ‚Äî the direct quality analogue; our exchange policy is better
  3. Pagerie (for aspirational buyers who baulked at $152) ‚Äî we are "Pagerie at a real-world price"
Key Message

The walk, put together.

(Secondary message: "At ‚Ç¨80, it costs less than a night out. And it will outlast both.")

Section 5: Pricing / Packaging Hypothesis

Anchor Pricing

Pagerie at $152 is the aspirational ceiling. Our ‚Ç¨80 is "everything Pagerie buyers wanted ‚Äî leather aesthetic, Italian craft, the look ‚Äî at a price that doesn't require a return drama to justify."

Price Positioning

Premium. Not accessible-budget (‚Ç¨15‚Äì30), not ultra-luxury (‚Ç¨150+). The premium craft tier (‚Ç¨60‚Äì120) is the real white space.

Rationale
  1. Competitive gap: No brand owns ‚Ç¨60‚Äì100 premium fashion-forward dog accessories in the EU market.

LISH is the closest analogue at ¬£65 but has operational failures and limited distribution.

  1. Willingness-to-pay evidence: Pagerie reviews show buyers comfortable at $152 for the concept;

the only complaints are about execution (returns, sizing), not sticker price.

  1. Same-body supply chain: Using the same mini bag body as HBAG (cost structure established)

makes ‚Ç¨80 viable at expected contribution margin (‚â•35% target, subject to TASK-03 supplier cost).

  1. Etsy artisan premium ceiling: Premium leather Etsy sellers top out at $50‚Äì60. ‚Ç¨80 requires

brand context beyond Etsy ‚Äî which the Instagram/TikTok probe tests directly.

Confidence Level

MEDIUM. Evidence supports ‚Ç¨80 as viable for a buyer who understands the brand. The risk: Etsy buyers may not have sufficient context from a listing alone to justify ‚Ç¨80 without seeing the brand story. Instagram/TikTok probe tests whether brand context drives price acceptance beyond the Etsy listing frame.

What would make this HIGH confidence: 3 paid sales at ‚Ç¨80 with no price objections in DMs.

Validation Plan
  1. TASK-06/07: Open Etsy listing at ‚Ç¨80; run Instagram probe for 28 days.
  2. Track: Do DM inquirers ask "is this the price?" (price shock signal) or move straight to "how

do I buy?" (acceptance signal).

  1. Checkpoint at 28 days: if 0 sales and DM inquiries include price objections, test ‚Ç¨65 for

2 weeks before concluding demand is absent.

  1. If 3+ sales at ‚Ç¨80 with no price complaints: confidence moves to HIGH; pricing confirmed.

A2: Naming territory map

1. Italian artisan provenance, without "atelier/maison" Opportunity: signal "made-with-care" and European taste through phonetics (soft vowels, clean consonants) rather than overused luxury words. Aligns with the competitive set where Italian brands combine craft cues with place names, but leaves room to avoid words like "atelier" or "maison" in the actual name.

2. Urban promenade / caf√©-terrazza world Opportunity: treat the walk as a "daily style ritual" (streets ‚Üí park ‚Üí espresso stop). Names should evoke movement, ease, and polish ‚Äî not utility. This sits apart from competitor names anchored in product category language such as "dog" or functional accessories.

3. Accessory-first fashion language Opportunity: position products like small leather goods (the way a mini bag or keychain charm is styled). Differentiates from competitors whose naming reads like pet gear ("Pet Company") or playful pet culture.

4. Subtle companionship (no dog/pet cue in name) Opportunity: build a brand the owner can hold without signalling "pet product," supporting future expansion into owner-facing accessories and travel/grooming bags. Structurally rarer in the competitor list, which often foregrounds "dog/pet/animal."

5. Warm feminine persona / founder-style label Opportunity: create a "person with taste" feeling ‚Äî approachable premium, compliments-friendly, social-handle-friendly. White space exists for founder energy without casualness (not cute, not twee).

A3: Landscape summary

The category is crowded with names that either (a) explicitly anchor to "dog/pet/animal," (b) use generic brand scaffolding ("Company," "& Co"), or (c) lean into pet-culture slang (e.g. "woof"), which tends to read more casual than the ‚Ç¨60‚Äì‚Ç¨150 premium band.

A second cluster borrows credibility via geography ("London," "Milano"), a proven shortcut to "style," but one that can become non-ownable ‚Äî especially when paired with descriptive category language.

White space for this positioning is clearest in fashion-label-first naming: short, elegant, vowel-friendly names that can sit on leather goods and jewellery-like charms without saying "dog," while still being pronounceable in English/Italian/French/Spanish. This also supports the key differentiator (premium craft at accessible-premium with a friendlier exchange policy) by signalling polish and trust rather than "pet novelty." Pagerie's narrow returns window and store-credit framing illustrates why a brand that feels welcoming and confident ‚Äî not punitive ‚Äî can win mindshare at the premium edge.

Underserved territories: Accessory-first fashion language and Subtle companionship are the most open; no current competitor clearly occupies either space.

B2: Per-candidate detail blocks
Vellara

Rationale: Vellara sounds like a small leather-goods label ‚Äî soft vowels, clean consonants, and a premium "hand-feel" in the mouth. It avoids pet clich√©s while still feeling warm and curated, fitting an urban millennial customer who wants the walk to feel styled rather than utilitarian. It scales: it could sit on collar charms, travel pouches, grooming bags, or owner accessories without sounding anchored to one product. Domain evidence: WHOIS not run; result: unknown ‚Äî check required; prioritise vellara.com, then vellara.co / vellara.eu. Trademark evidence: EUIPO eSearch + UKIPO; query: "Vellara"; classes searched: 18, 28, 35, 25, 14; closest match: unknown ‚Äî search blocked; manual check required; risk: unknown ‚Äî search blocked; manual check required. Handle evidence: @vellara Instagram: unknown ‚Äî check required; @vellara.dog Instagram: unknown ‚Äî check required; @vellara TikTok: unknown ‚Äî check required. Pronunciation notes: Likely "veh-LAR-uh." Works in English; feels natural with Italian/French vowel patterns; Spanish straightforward. Mild spelling-variant risk (Velara / Vellara). Linguistic check: English: No obvious negative meaning; mild spelling variant risk. Italian: No negative meaning; reads plausibly Italian-adjacent. French: No negative meaning; may soften the "a" but still clear. Spanish: No negative meaning; likely pronounced cleanly. Brand story potential: "A label for the daily promenade ‚Äî small leather pieces that make you feel put together."

D) Recommendation

Recommended name: Vellara

Vellara is the strongest fit for the "premium dog lifestyle accessories" positioning because it behaves like a fashion label first and a pet brand second ‚Äî exactly the white space that emerges when examining the competitor landscape. Many competitors either foreground pet category language ("Dog/Pet/Animal"), lean casual/playful ("woof"), or rely on structural scaffolding such as "Company/& Co," which pulls perceived tone downmarket relative to the ‚Ç¨60‚Äì‚Ç¨150 goal.

Vellara is short, vowel-friendly, and easy to place on leather goods, charms, travel pouches, grooming accessories, and eventually owner accessories ‚Äî without sounding like a single-product brand. It supports the emotional and social job-to-be-done: the name feels "curated and confident," consistent with "I'm the dog mum who has it together."

Crucially, the sound and temperament of Vellara communicates trust and warmth rather than exclusivity-as-punishment. That matters because a core premium-category pain point is returns rigidity ‚Äî Pagerie's narrow returns window and store-credit framing makes buyers feel stuck. The planned 30-day no-fault exchange becomes more believable under a name that feels welcoming, not severe. The invented quality of the word also means SERP noise risk is low ‚Äî no competing dictionary meaning floods results ‚Äî and the invented construction leaves room for trademark ownership across the product roadmap classes.

Suggested tagline / brand descriptor: City-walk essentials, finished like jewellery.

Primary risk: Trademark and handle/domain clearance is unverified (EUIPO and UKIPO search was blocked during research). Before committing, run manual clearance: EUIPO eSearch + UKIPO in classes 18/28/35/25/14; verify @vellara and @vellara.dog on Instagram and @vellara on TikTok; and secure vellara.com (or vellara.co / vellara.eu as fallback).

Two alternatives if Vellara hits a blocker: Lunera, Civana.

90-Day Forecast v2

docs/business-os/strategy/PET/italy-90-day-launch-forecast-v2.user.md

PET Italy 90-Day Launch Forecast (v2)

Decision Frame

  • Decision owner: Pete
  • Decision: whether to launch PET SKU1 now on own-site DTC, with paid used as learning + retargeting
  • Decision date: 2026-02-11
  • Scope: first 90 days only, Italy market only, SKU1-led launch

What Changed vs v1

  • Forecast is now channel-causal (paid spend -&gt; CPC -&gt; paid sessions) instead of independent volume assumptions.
  • Unit economics now includes variable costs beyond COGS.
  • Explicit week-2 go/no-go gates are defined.
  • Inventory capacity is treated as a hard constraint, not implied.

Model Mechanics

Core formulas
  • Paid sessions = Ad spend / CPC
  • Total sessions = Paid sessions + Organic/Creator/Referral sessions
  • Orders = Total sessions * CVR
  • Net revenue (ex VAT) = Orders * (AOV incl VAT / 1.22)
  • Contribution/order (pre ads) = Net AOV - (COGS + fulfillment + payment fee + returns reserve + shipping subsidy)
  • Contribution after ads = Orders * Contribution/order - Ad spend
  • Blended CAC = Ad spend / Orders
Hard constants
  • VAT: 22%
  • SKU1 COGS: EUR 2.00 (given)

Scenario Inputs (Assumptions)

InputP10P50P90Notes
Ad spend (90d)EUR 600EUR 1,800EUR 3,500learning + retargeting bias
CPCEUR 0.90EUR 0.70EUR 0.55planning assumptions; replace with observed
Organic/creator/referral sessions3,3009,30015,600depends on creator output + distribution
CVR1.0%1.5%2.2%anchored to prior Italy benchmark band
AOV (incl VAT)EUR 31EUR 33EUR 35includes occasional shipping/add-on effects
Fulfillment + packaging/orderEUR 4.80EUR 4.80EUR 4.80assumption
Payment fee/orderEUR 1.28EUR 1.34EUR 1.40assumption (blended)
Returns reserve/orderEUR 1.52EUR 1.62EUR 1.72assumption
Shipping subsidy/orderEUR 1.50EUR 1.50EUR 1.50assumption

90-Day Output Forecast

MetricP10P50P90
Paid sessions (derived)6672,5716,364
Total sessions (derived)3,96711,87121,964
Orders (derived)40178483
Gross revenue incl VAT (derived)EUR 1,240EUR 5,874EUR 16,905
Net revenue ex VAT (derived)EUR 1,016EUR 4,815EUR 13,857
Contribution/order pre ads (derived)EUR 14.31EUR 15.79EUR 17.27
Contribution pre ads (derived)EUR 572EUR 2,811EUR 8,341
Contribution after ads (derived)EUR -28EUR 1,011EUR 4,841
Blended CAC (derived)EUR 15.00EUR 10.11EUR 7.25

Week-2 Recalibration Gates (Mandatory)

Scale only if all pass:

  1. CVR (7-day trailing) &gt;= 1.2%
  2. Blended CAC &lt;= 70% of observed contribution/order pre ads
  3. Refund rate &lt;= 8%
  4. On-time ship rate &gt;= 95%
  5. Payment success rate &gt;= 97%

If any gate fails, switch to fix-first mode:

  • stop cold acquisition expansion
  • keep retargeting only
  • run focused PDP/checkout/shipping-trust experiments
  • re-forecast remaining 10 weeks using observed data
Gate validity rules (minimum denominators)
  • CVR gate is decision-valid only when sessions &gt;= 500 and orders &gt;= 10.
  • Refund gate is decision-valid only when orders_shipped &gt;= 25.
  • Payment-success gate is decision-valid only when payment_attempts &gt;= 100.
  • If a denominator is below threshold, mark result as insufficient-sample and extend observation window before scale decisions.
Gate ownership and re-test SLA
  • Demand efficiency gates (CVR, CAC): growth owner.
  • Reliability gates (refund, on-time ship, payment success): operations owner.
  • Any failed gate requires a named owner, remediation plan within 48 hours, and re-test within 7 days.

Inventory Constraint (Critical Unknown)

  • P90 requires capacity for ~483 shipped orders in 90 days.
  • If available sellable units are below scenario demand, cap orders at inventory and recompute CAC/contribution.
  • Forecast is not decision-grade until current on-hand + in-transit units are confirmed.

Priority Risks and Mitigations

RiskWhy it breaks forecastMitigation
CAC inflationdestroys contribution at low AOVretargeting-first, fast creative pruning, strict CAC gate
Conversion underperformancelow order volume despite trafficsimplify PDP/checkout, improve shipping/returns clarity
Returns spikeerodes margin and cash flowtighter fit/use expectations, explicit product dimensions, usage proof
Inventory delay/shortageconstrains realizable revenuepre-order transparency + inventory-capped weekly lp-do-replan
Benchmark stalenesswrong priors for decisioningrefresh market/CVR references during week-2 recalibration

Required Data to Upgrade v2 -> Decision-Grade

  1. Confirm inventory units and arrival dates.
  2. Capture real blended payment + fulfillment cost per order.
  3. Replace benchmark CPC/CVR priors with observed week-1 and week-2 data.
  4. Recompute CAC ceiling from observed contribution/order.

Operational Next 14 Days

  1. Instrument funnel events end-to-end and validate against real test orders.
  2. Run 10-15 creatives/week and cut bottom quartile every 72 hours.
  3. Track daily dashboard: sessions, CVR, CAC, refund %, payment success, on-time ship.
  4. Execute week-2 go/no-go decision with revised 10-week forecast.

Market Intelligence (Resolved)

T2 ¬∑ 240 lines

docs/business-os/market-research/PET/2026-02-12-market-intelligence.user.md

PET Market Intelligence Pack (Italy)

A) Executive Summary

  • Italy has a large dog-owner base: about 28% of households own at least one dog.
  • Using 26.5m families (2024), implied dog-owning households are ~7.42m.
  • Price ladder is wide: low-end dispensers near EUR1.99 through premium leather and design-led options, up to luxury anchors.
  • Commodity patterns are clear: leash attachment, side dispensing opening, included bags at lower price points.
  • Review-led failure modes in lower tiers are explicit: closure failure, hook breakage, roll loss.
  • Premium-aesthetic wedge exists and is active in Italy-accessible channels.
  • TikTok Shop is live in Italy and materially improves speed-to-first-sales in pre-website mode.
  • Italian checkout expectations require broad payment methods; wallets are significant.
  • Competitor shipping thresholds cluster around ~EUR49-67, indicating proven bundle-to-threshold mechanics.
  • Biodegradable/compostable bag claims are sensitive: compatibility and substantiated standards language matter.
  • Best 90-day path is pre-website social commerce + minimal buy-link surface, then deeper site build only after proof.
  • Strategic moat is likely design + reliability + clean-carry experience, not commodity dispenser pricing.

B) Business Context and Assumptions

Observed context from intake:

  • Business: PET.
  • Product lane: handbag-style poop bag holder, then biodegradable bags.
  • First audience hypothesis: female pet owners.
  • Product inventory for first SKU already purchased; expected in <=20 days.
  • Primary long-term channel intent: own ecommerce site.
  • Current launch surface: pre-website.
  • Non-negotiables: speed-to-first-sales and no over-building.

Key assumptions used in this pack:

  • Initial holder test pricing range: EUR18-30 incl. VAT (premium-accessible tier).
  • Handbag-style still requires practical default attachment behavior.
  • Early paid spend is validation spend, not scale economics.

C) Market Size and Demand Signals

SignalWhat it means for PET
28% dog-owning households (Italy)Large baseline market for dog-walk accessories
26.5m Italian families (2024)Useful denominator for TAM sizing
~7.42m implied dog-owner householdsPractical demand planning baseline
~8.8m dogs (cited country table)Supports repeat consumables lane (bags)
Large review volume on poop bags/dispenser listingsConsumable repeat category appears high-velocity
TikTok Shop Italy launch + large user reachStrong pre-website transaction channel for rapid validation

Seasonality confidence remains low with current evidence; run short-cycle tests instead of relying on assumptions.

D) Competitor and Substitute Map

Direct and near-direct:

  • zooplus / Trixie / Earth Rated / United Pets / L'Isola dei Tesori / MatiMati.
  • Amazon marketplace holders (including leather-style options).
  • Design-led DTC analogues (MiaCara, Timoteo Milano).

Adjacent and substitute signals:

  • Walk-kit pouch products with integrated dispensers.
  • Luxury fashion-pet accessories (price anchoring more than volume competition).

Core strategic takeaway:

  • Avoid commodity price competition.
  • Differentiate with premium aesthetics plus explicit reliability proof and cleaner carry UX.

E) Pricing and Offer Benchmarks

Observed pricing ladder (Italy-accessible):

  • Utility low-end: ~EUR1.99-6.99.
  • Mid / premium-accessible: ~EUR19.99-29.95.
  • Higher premium Italian leather examples around ~EUR54.
  • Luxury anchor examples far above mass-premium.

Observed commercial patterns:

  • Included starter bags are common in lower tiers.
  • Cross-sell / bundle mechanics are common.
  • Free-shipping thresholds around ~EUR49-67 appear repeatedly.

F) Segments and JTBD Sequence

Primary segment (first 90 days):

  • Urban style-forward female dog owners (daily walkers).
  • JTBD: fast clean bag access in a product that feels like a real accessory, without cheap failure modes.

Secondary segment:

  • New puppy/dog owners buying walk essentials.
  • JTBD: simple starter set with low decision friction.

Tertiary segment:

  • Dog walkers/sitters who value reliability and speed in repeated daily use.

G) Unit Economics Priors (Validation Stage)

These are priors to validate in first 14 days:

MetricPrior range / posture
Holder AOVEUR18-30 (assumption)
Bundle AOV (holder + bags)EUR25-40 (assumption)
CVR baseline referenceLow single-digit benchmark range; validate quickly in-channel
Cart abandonment baselineUse benchmark as warning threshold, not forecast certainty
ReturnsAssume lower than apparel but non-trivial; validate with reason coding
Paid CACTreat as uncertain until channel and creative data are measured
Gross/contribution marginPotentially strong on holder COGS, but fragile to shipping/refunds/CAC

H) Channel Strategy (First 90 Days)

Recommended sequence:

  1. Launch in pre-website stack:
  • TikTok Shop + creator content + LIVE.
  • Buy-link commerce surface for non-TikTok traffic.
  • Instagram shopping/discovery support.
  1. Introduce bags as bundle/subscription repeat mechanism once first holder demand is validated.
  2. Build deeper owned-site depth only after conversion/objection evidence is clear.
  3. Optional marketplace expansion only if it does not slow primary speed-to-sales loop.

I) Website / PDP Implications

Minimum viable conversion surface requirements:

  • Clear product proposition above the fold:
  • stylish,
  • reliable,
  • clean-carry.
  • Explicit dimensions + standard-roll compatibility.
  • Refill/how-to content (short video/gif).
  • Clear inclusion statement (bags included or not).
  • Delivery timing and shipping policy clarity.
  • Payment breadth appropriate for Italy.
  • Returns/withdrawal policy clarity.
  • Fast-response support channel (including messaging app support).

J) Product Implications

Must-have design criteria:

  • Durable attachment hardware.
  • Reliable closure (no accidental opening).
  • Smooth single-bag dispensing.
  • Explicit roll compatibility.
  • Premium carry experience (quiet, clean, non-dangling feel).

Early failure modes to test out:

  • closure opening unexpectedly,
  • clip/hook failure,
  • roll fit incompatibility,
  • material/finish durability under daily outdoor use.

K) Regulatory and Claims Constraints

Key constraints to apply:

  • GPSR obligations are active and relevant to online/offline consumer sales.
  • Italy/EU withdrawal rights and consumer guarantees must be reflected in policy.
  • Italian packaging environmental labeling obligations must be handled correctly.
  • Green claims on bags (biodegradable/compostable) require precise, substantiated wording and condition clarity.

Red lines:

  1. Do not use vague or unsubstantiated environmental claims.
  2. Do not ship without compliant policy + labeling setup.
  3. Do not scale before product reliability failure modes are controlled.

L) 90-Day Outcome Contract (Proposed)

OutcomeTarget window
First paid order from pre-website surfaceDay 7
Price-point willingness validationDay 14
Bags attach-rate / repeat path signalDay 45
Contribution margin proof-of-lifeDay 60
Creator loop proving repeatable acquisitionDay 90

M) First-14-Day Validation Tests

  1. Price A/B on pre-website surface.
  2. Offer test: holder-only vs starter set.
  3. Messaging split: fashion-first vs reliability-first.
  4. UGC proof test for function + carry experience.
  5. Checkout friction test across payment methods.
  6. Durability red-team stress test before scaling spend.

Each test should have explicit pass/fail thresholds and clear re-forecast triggers.

N) Assumptions Register (Condensed)

Highest-impact assumptions:

  • premium-accessible pricing will convert,
  • TikTok Shop will be fastest initial channel,
  • returns can remain controlled for this accessory type,
  • reliability messaging will outperform pure-aesthetic in paid performance,
  • bags attach-rate can create early repeat economics.

O) Risk Register (Condensed)

Top risks:

  • category commoditization and price-floor pressure,
  • hardware failure creating negative review loops,
  • compliance exposure from weak green claims,
  • payment-method friction reducing completion,
  • operational time loss from over-building before proof.

Site Upgrade Brief (Resolved)

T2 ¬∑ 142 lines

docs/business-os/site-upgrades/PET/2026-02-12-upgrade-brief.user.md

PET Site Upgrade Brief

1) Business Outcome Frame

  • Convert first PET demand into reliable sales using a fast pre-website surface, then harden into repeatable DTC.
  • Maximize conversion on a style-led but utility-critical product (poop bag holder) while minimizing returns and support load.
  • Decision links unlocked:
  • DEC-PET-01: scale traffic and channel investment after first conversion proof.
  • DEC-PET-02: expand bundle/recurring bag economics once holder conversion is stable.

2) Existing Site Baseline

  • Launch-surface mode: pre-website.
  • Core constraint: speed-to-first-sales; avoid heavy build before proof.
  • Current friction risks to remove before scale:
  • weak trust signals for a new brand,
  • unclear fit/compatibility on bag roll formats,
  • weak bundle and quick-add UX,
  • checkout/payment friction for Italy.

3) Reference Sites

  • MiaCara: premium-accessory PDP discipline (fit/details/trust).
  • Labbvenn: material quality framing + incentives.
  • Poldo Dog Couture: Italian premium signal and origin trust.
  • A.Mici&Co Boutique: quick-cart and localized merchandising.
  • Sezane, Missoma, Astrid & Miyu, Monica Vinader: fashion-grade DTC trust, quick-add, bundles/sets, and post-purchase confidence patterns.

4) Pattern Decomposition

Reference sitePatternWhy it mattersEvidence
MiaCaraStrong PDP structure (dimensions, promise, accessory context)Reduces uncertainty on a functional accessory sold at premium aestheticsDeep research pattern code: V&gt;F&gt;T&gt;B&gt;P&gt;Q
LabbvennMaterial-quality framing + offer nudgeSupports premium positioning while retaining conversion intentDeep research pattern code: I&gt;F&gt;P&gt;T&gt;B&gt;Q
Poldo Dog CoutureMade-in-Italy trust and premium signalHelps PET if origin/story is part of offerDeep research pattern code: O&gt;T&gt;Q&gt;I&gt;C&gt;B
A.Mici&CoQuick-cart behavior in localized pet contextFaster purchase path and less PDP drop-offDeep research pattern code: Q&gt;V&gt;T&gt;B&gt;I&gt;F

6) Design Implications

  • Information architecture:
  • Home (style + utility split),
  • Core holder PDP,
  • Bundle PDP (holder + bags),
  • Support/FAQ,
  • Shipping/returns/legal.
  • Page/component implications:
  • trust strip near CTA,
  • explicit fit block (dimensions + compatible roll format),
  • quick add / sticky mobile add-to-cart,
  • bundle selector.
  • Copy/messaging implications:
  • combine aesthetic language with reliability claims (secure closure, easy dispense, clean carry),
  • avoid vague green claims for bags without substantiation.
  • Trust/support implications:
  • clear delivery window and tracking promise,
  • clear returns/withdrawal workflow,
  • visible support channel for pre-purchase questions.

7) Technical Implications

  • Reusable platform primitives to use:
  • product option controls,
  • quick-cart/sticky CTA component,
  • trust strip block,
  • FAQ and policy components.
  • New build requirements:
  • explicit fit/compatibility field model (holder dimensions, roll format compatibility),
  • bundle pricing rule engine for holder+bags packs,
  • event instrumentation for quick add, bundle selection, and checkout drop-off.
  • Testing and observability implications:
  • unit tests for bundle/price logic,
  • integration tests for option and quick-add flows,
  • E2E tests for checkout and policy visibility,
  • funnel analytics with conversion by message/offer variant.

8) Prioritized Backlog Candidates

9) Open Questions

  • What exact roll formats will be guaranteed compatible at launch?
  • Will bags be included in-box by default or only as bundle add-on?
  • What first-cycle shipping SLA can be promised reliably in Italy?
  • Which payment methods are confirmed day one (cards, wallets, PayPal, prepaid-friendly)?
  • Which support channel SLA can be maintained in week 1-4?

Pet Product ‚Äî Brand Dossier

> Draft status. This dossier was bootstrapped from the business plan and forecast. > No app or theme package exists yet. All visual identity fields are TBD with rationale. > The category has not yet been narrowed from the broader "pet products" space ‚Äî > brand identity cannot be fully resolved until the primary product category is locked. > All TBD fields require operator input after Category and Segment Prioritization (plan ¬ßStrategy item 2).

Audience

Primary: TBD ‚Äî pet owners in Italy. The specific pet type (dogs, cats, small animals) and the owner profile (age, lifestyle, purchase motivation) must be resolved as part of Category and Segment Prioritization.

Secondary: TBD ‚Äî gift purchasers, specialty pet retailers (if wholesale applies).

Device: TBD ‚Äî assumed mobile-first based on Italian e-commerce norms and comparable category benchmarks, but must be validated with first-party data.

Context: TBD ‚Äî depends on the product category selected. High-intent search acquisition is planned; social (Instagram/TikTok for visual pet content) is a likely secondary channel. Emotional purchase drivers are expected (pet owners have strong affiliation with their animals); practical drivers (price, compatibility, safety) also apply.

Key constraint: Brand positioning cannot be completed until the product category is locked. "Pet Product" is a placeholder ‚Äî the audience is different for dog accessories vs. cat toys vs. small-animal nutrition.

Personality

> TBD ‚Äî Directional candidates pending category lock: > - If accessories (leash, collar, harness): Practical + stylish, approachable, quality-forward > - If nutrition/treats: Trustworthy + caring, clean-ingredient focus, reassuring > - If toys/enrichment: Playful + warm, energetic, fun > > Validate personality direction after category lock and ‚â•3 customer/community inputs.

Common to all candidate directions:

  • Warm, not clinical (pet owners have emotional relationships with their animals)
  • Approachable, not pretentious
  • Italy-native, not translated from English templates

PET Forecast Seed for SFS-00

0a) Business-Now (Outcome Contract Proposal)

  • Outcome-ID: PET-OUT-2026Q1-01
  • Outcome statement: Achieve first reliable direct sales for PET in Italy via pre-website launch surfaces, then convert validated demand into owned-site growth with sustainable unit economics.
  • Baseline (2026-02-12):
  • paid orders: 0
  • net revenue: EUR 0
  • blended CAC: not measured
  • return rate: not measured
  • Target (90 days):
  • orders: 178 (forecast P50)
  • gross revenue incl VAT: EUR 5,874 (forecast P50)
  • blended CAC: <=EUR 10-12 by day 60-90 (subject to contribution guardrail)
  • return rate: <=8%
  • By (deadline): 2026-05-13
  • Owner: Pete
  • Leading indicators (weekly):
  • sessions by channel (TikTok Shop / buy-link / organic / paid)
  • CVR by channel
  • paid CAC and blended CAC
  • payment success rate
  • on-time ship rate
  • return reason distribution
  • Decision link: DEC-PET-01 (whether to scale spend/channel breadth beyond validation mode)
  • Stop/Pivot guardrails:
  • if CVR <1.2% after sufficient sample, fix conversion before spend increase
  • if blended CAC >70% of observed contribution/order pre-ads, stop expansion and run fix-first loop
  • if return rate >8% or on-time ship <95%, hold growth and remediate operations

0b) Existing-Work-Now (From Current Evidence)

Confirmed available now:

  • Product lane and first SKU direction: handbag-style poop bag holder
  • Follow-on SKU direction: biodegradable/compostable bag lane
  • Initial audience hypothesis: female pet owners
  • Inventory posture: first SKU stock purchased; expected in <=20 days
  • Market intelligence baseline: docs/business-os/market-research/PET/2026-02-12-market-intelligence.user.md
  • Forecast baseline: docs/business-os/strategy/PET/italy-90-day-launch-forecast-v2.user.md

Still missing / needs confirmation:

  • exact sellable units and confirmed first in-stock date
  • final price architecture (single, bundle, and any shipping threshold strategy)
  • validated closure/hardware durability pass criteria for SKU1
  • payment stack readiness checklist and live checkout test status
  • returns flow copy and operational SLA confirmation
  • packaging/environmental labeling compliance checklist for Italy

0c) Merge + Classification for First Execution Pack

Reuse-existing:

  • channel and economics model from italy-90-day-launch-forecast-v2.user.md
  • segment and positioning evidence from 2026-02-12-market-intelligence.user.md

Adapt-existing:

  • convert priors into a live weekly PET launch scorecard with measured thresholds
  • split offer testing into explicit matrix (price x message x bundle)

New required artifacts:

  • PET launch scorecard (weekly live metrics)
  • offer-test matrix (price/messaging/bundle variants)
  • durability and returns root-cause tracker
  • payment and shipping reliability checklist

Ready-to-Execute Go Items (Seed)

  1. Launch pre-website conversion surface with full event and checkout instrumentation.
  2. Run week-1 price and messaging tests (fashion-first vs reliability-first) with strict pass/fail thresholds.
  3. Validate operations gates (payment success, ship SLA, return reasons) before scale.
  4. Hold week-2 recalibration and re-forecast the remaining 10 weeks using observed data.

Week 2 Gate Dry-Run

T3 ¬∑ 88 lines

docs/business-os/strategy/PET/2026-02-11-week2-gate-dry-run.user.md

PET Week-2 Gate Review ‚Äî Dry-Run (Synthetic)

Purpose

Validate that the launch decision process is correctly configured and produces useful decisions before the website is launch-ready.

Inputs Used (Synthetic)

Assumed 7-day trailing observed metrics:

MetricDry-run valueGate
CVR1.43%>= 1.2%
Contribution/order (pre ads)EUR 15.79baseline
Blended CACEUR 8.57<= 70% of contribution/order (<= EUR 11.05)
Refund rate5.5%<= 8%
On-time ship rate92.0%>= 95%
Payment success rate98.1%>= 97%

Gate Evaluation

GateResultNotes
CVR >= 1.2%PASSDemand conversion acceptable
CAC <= 70% of contribution/orderPASSAcquisition efficiency acceptable
Refund <= 8%PASSReturn burden controlled
On-time ship >= 95%FAILFulfillment execution below threshold
Payment success >= 97%PASSCheckout reliability acceptable

Decision rule outcome:

  • NO-GO (scale hold) because one mandatory gate failed.
  • Prescribed action from v2 process: fix-first mode (hold cold scale, keep retargeting, run shipping trust + ops fixes, re-test next 7 days).

Quality Check ‚Äî Is This Setup Right and Valuable?

Rubric
DimensionScore (0-5)Why
Deterministic decisioning5.0Hard numeric gates produce repeatable pass/fail outcomes
Actionability4.5Explicit fallback mode is defined when any gate fails
Margin protection4.5CAC threshold tied to contribution prevents false-positive scale
Operational risk capture5.0Shipping SLA gate blocks unsafe scaling despite good demand metrics
Data burden realism3.5Requires reliable daily instrumentation not yet proven live
Anti-vanity bias5.0Avoids scaling from top-line metrics alone

Weighted quality score:

  • 4.6 / 5.0 (92%)
Value Demonstrated by This Dry-Run
  • Without this gate system, the team would likely scale (CVR/CAC look good).
  • The process correctly blocks scale due to a fulfillment reliability failure (92% vs required 95%).
  • This is exactly the intended behavior: preserve trust and contribution before expansion.

Gaps Found in the Process Setup

  1. Minimum sample-size rule coverage was missing at review time. Resolved in docs/business-os/strategy/PET/italy-90-day-launch-forecast-v2.user.md.
  2. No explicit confidence interval/variance handling is defined for low-volume weeks. Open.
  3. Failed-gate owner/SLA assignment was missing at review time. Resolved in docs/business-os/strategy/PET/italy-90-day-launch-forecast-v2.user.md.

Patch Recommendations (Process-Level)

  1. Add minimum denominator rules:
  • CVR gate valid only if sessions &gt;= 500 and orders &gt;= 10.
  • Refund gate valid only if orders_shipped &gt;= 25.
  1. Add gate ownership:
  • Demand gates: growth owner.
  • Ops gates: fulfillment owner.
  1. Add a re-test SLA:
  • after fail, re-test within 7 days with explicit recovery target.

Conclusion

This process is configured well enough to add real decision value in pre-launch dry-runs. After same-day patches, only variance/confidence handling remains open before live scaling decisions.

Strategy Plan

T1 ¬∑ 172 lines

docs/business-os/strategy/BRIK/plan.user.md

Brikette ‚Äî Business Plan

Business overview

Brikette is a physical hostel in Positano on the Amalfi Coast. The ambition is to be the most expensive hostel in the world while remaining very busy ‚Äî premium pricing justified by exceptional quality across every dimension: comfortable rooms, great common areas, great staff and service, organised activities, and deep local knowledge delivered to guests. This is not a budget product with an inflated price; it is a genuinely excellent hospitality product that earns its premium.

Revenue lines, all part of the same physical hospitality business:

  • Hostel bookings ‚Äî room nights across 11 rooms in a multi-locale market, currently sold via OTA and direct
  • Experiences and activities ‚Äî organised activities and local knowledge as a product, not a free add-on
  • StepFree Chiesa Nuova apartment ‚Äî a 100sqm apartment adjacent to the hostel (new for 2026), targeting couples, listed on Booking.com only so far

The digital platform (brikette website, content guides, reception app) is infrastructure that supports the physical business ‚Äî it is not the business itself.

Strategy

Current Focus (2026-02-17)
  1. L3 Transition: Reception Infrastructure (Priority: High)
  • Status: Building reception app with live till, loan items, shift management; addressing Firebase prerender errors and client boundary issues
  • Next: Complete BRIK-ENG-0018 (Dashboard Upgrade Aggregator) to unify reception metrics
  1. Analytics & Visibility Gap (Priority: High)
  • Status: GA4 admin settings are verified (referral exclusion and cross-domain suggestions reviewed), and debug validation confirms begin_checkout can fire under consent-granted test conditions
  • Next: Verify non-zero handoff event counts in standard Data API windows and complete governance runbook (handoff_to_engine, conversion mapping, weekly review cadence)
  1. Content Commerce Maturity (Priority: Medium)
  • Status: 168+ guides across 18 locales operational; Cloudflare staging deployed (staging.brikette-website.pages.dev)
  • Next: Validate guide translation quality, establish content update workflow
  1. Booking Funnel Recovery (Octorate Last-Mile Model) (Priority: High)
  • Status: Fact-find and sequenced plan completed with no-API scope confirmed (BRIK-ENG-0021)
  • Next: Execute foundation tasks in validated order: native handoff_to_engine emission (TASK-05A) -> same-tab normalization (TASK-03) -> GA4 governance parity (TASK-06) -> overlap-window reconciliation calibration (TASK-08)

Startup-Loop Outcome Contract (Canonical)

Promoted from:

  • docs/business-os/startup-baselines/BRIK-forecast-seed.user.md
  • docs/business-os/strategy/BRIK/2026-02-13-startup-loop-90-day-forecast-v1.user.md

  • Outcome-ID: BRIK-OUT-2026Q2-01
  • Outcome statement: Grow Brikette's net booking value and revenue per available bed over the next 90 days ‚Äî establishing the measurement and operational foundation needed to price, fill, and operate at the premium level the product ambition demands.
  • Baseline (2026-02-13):
  • trailing 90-day net booking value (2025-11..2026-01): EUR 28,927.79
  • trailing 90-day bookings (2025-11..2026-01): 100
  • direct booking share (same window): 18%
  • paid CAC: not measured at decision-grade quality
  • Operational data baseline (2026-02-14):
  • Octorate calendar export: Mar 2025 - Oct 2026 (18 months, 612 date rows)
  • Room inventory: 11 total rooms (9 numbered: 3-6, 8-12; 2 year-named: 2022-7, 2025-14)
  • Data sheets: Price, Availability, Length of stay, Real availability
  • Source: data/octorate/octorate-calendar-2026-02-14.xlsx + metadata JSONs
  • Automation: ‚úÖ Fully automated via packages/mcp-server/octorate-export-final-working.mjs
  • Protocol: docs/business-os/startup-loop/octorate-data-collection-protocol.md
  • Target (90 days, by 2026-05-13):
  • net booking value: EUR 205,200 (forecast P50)
  • bookings: 760 (forecast P50)
  • direct booking share: 27% (forecast P50)
  • paid CAC: <=EUR 95 by day 14 and <=EUR 90 by day 60-90
  • Leading indicators (weekly):
  • tracked sessions
  • session-to-booking CVR
  • paid CAC and spend efficiency
  • direct share vs OTA share
  • booking-step p75 performance
  • cancellation reason coding coverage
  • Decision link: DEC-BRIK-02 (whether BRIK has recovered into a reliable positive trend and can scale controlled growth investments)
Guardrails
  • If CVR <1.2% after >=5,000 sessions, hold spend expansion and prioritize funnel fixes.
  • If paid CAC >EUR 130 for 7 consecutive days, reduce to retargeting-only mode.
  • If direct share <20% by day 14, accelerate member-rate/perk experiment and re-check margin impact.
  • If booking-step p75 load >3.0s for 3 consecutive days, freeze offer experiments until performance is restored.

Risks

Active Risks
  • Measurement Signal Quality Incomplete (Severity: Medium, Added: 2026-02-09, Updated: 2026-02-17)
  • Source: Event firing is observable in debug sessions, but standard report windows still show inconsistent/zero handoff coverage for decision use
  • Impact: Traffic baseline exists, but conversion decisioning remains partially blind until report-layer handoff visibility stabilizes
  • Mitigation: ship native handoff_to_engine instrumentation, validate in bounded windows, and enforce a weekly GA4 governance checklist
  • Booking Completion Attribution Gap (No API/Webhook Access) (Severity: Medium, Added: 2026-02-17)
  • Source: Octorate API/webhook onboarding is unavailable in this phase; deterministic join key closure is not yet feasible
  • Impact: End-to-end revenue attribution is probabilistic and can lag operational decisions
  • Mitigation: run no-API reconciliation (aggregate + probabilistic) weekly with explicit confidence thresholds and caveat labeling
  • Translation Quality Unknown (Severity: Medium, Added: 2026-02-09)
  • Source: 168+ guides x 18 locales = 3,024 guide pages; structure-first translation workflow established but quality gates unvalidated at scale
  • Impact: Potential SEO penalties, user trust issues, booking conversion impact
  • Mitigation: Run strict-mode i18n audit, spot-check high-traffic guides, establish ongoing quality monitoring
  • Reception App Stability (Severity: Medium, Added: 2026-02-09)
  • Source: Recent Firebase prerender errors, client boundary issues (SafeDataContext, TillShiftProvider, Live.tsx, Till.tsx)
  • Impact: Reception staff workflow disruption, manual fallback required
  • Mitigation: Comprehensive error boundary strategy, server/client separation enforcement, monitoring

Without non-zero conversion-intent signal, the P50 scenario's core metric (1.9% CVR) is a historical analogy, not a measured fact for this funnel. Engineering work in brikette-cta-sales-funnel-ga4 is addressing the booking flow, but the upstream measurement closure has not been confirmed in a locked 7-day window yet.

How to Promote a Finding Brief

To act on a finding:

  1. Copy the Promotion stub from the Finding Brief you want to promote.
  2. Create a new file at docs/plans/&lt;finding-slug&gt;/fact-find.md.
  3. Paste the frontmatter stub. Fill remaining required fields from docs/plans/_templates/fact-find-planning.md.
  4. Add Fingerprint: &lt;fingerprint&gt; in the body (not in frontmatter).
  5. Run /lp-do-fact-find on the brief to complete the evidence audit and gap review.
  6. Once promoted, future Signal Reviews will suppress this fingerprint (dedup source: open plan tasks).

BRIK Startup-Loop 90-Day Forecast (v1)

Input Packet

  • Business: BRIK (Brikette)
  • Launch surface: website-live
  • Horizon: 90 days (2026-02-14 to 2026-05-13)
  • Core inputs:
  • docs/business-os/market-research/BRIK/2026-02-12-market-intelligence.user.md

  • docs/business-os/strategy/BRIK/2026-02-13-measurement-verification.user.md

Launch Surface Mode

  • Mode used: website-live
  • Forecast focus: sessions, bookings, net booking value, channel mix, and guardrails for paid/cancellation risk.
  • Constraint: GA4/Search Console core setup is now live, but event-level verification and first 7-day baseline are still in progress.
